        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1157110431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8412040466319272035">I while ago I read <i>Northanger Abbey</i> and while I enjoyed it I also felt like missing out on half of the jokes because while was vaguely aware that Gothic novels meant scary old castles, fair maidens and old curses I had never read one of them. So I eventually decided to read one (after buying it, putting it on my tbr-pile and forgetting about it again till yesterday).<br/>As it happens <i>The Castle of Otranto</i> is actually the first novel that (in its second edition) was published as "Gothic Novel" and wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8412040466319272035" style="display:none">I while ago I read <i>Northanger Abbey</i> and while I enjoyed it I also felt like missing out on half of the jokes because while was vaguely aware that Gothic novels meant scary old castles, fair maidens and old curses I had never read one of them. So I eventually decided to read one (after buying it, putting it on my tbr-pile and forgetting about it again till yesterday).<br />As it happens <i>The Castle of Otranto</i> is actually the first novel that (in its second edition) was published as "Gothic Novel" and wow! It certainly is one. Half a page in the only son and heir of Manfred, the highly unlikeable the lord of the castle has already kicked the bucket (only minutes before the wedding) after a piece of a statue (that apparently appeared out of nowhere) fell on him. Half a page later Manfred has already condemned an unsuspecting bystander to death who just remarked on the similarities between the piece and a statue in the castle and then tries to persuade Isabelle, his son's not-quite-widow to marry him (she refuses among other reasons because Manfred's wife is still alive). It continues in that speed and so the 100 pages are crammed with <i>everything</i>. Mistaken identities, birth-marks that reveal a person's true heritage, curses and enough murder, manipulation and bloodshed to keep up with many contemporary thrillers.<br />As a result it reads more like a parody that crams all kinds of Gothic tropes together than something that (at least to an extend) wanted to be taken seriously but it is definitely an enjoyable read and because of the shortness and the fact that it was the first Gothic novel not a bad place to start if you're also curious about Gothic fiction.<br /><br />This review also appears on <a href="http://aoife.booklikes.com/post/1079042/review-the-castle-of-otranto" rel="nofollow noopener">Witty Little Knitter</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_5507063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5507063" />
    <a title="A." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/334282-a"><img alt="A." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274108272p2/334282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5507063?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="A." href="/user/show/334282-a">A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140437676" href="/book/show/609044.The_Castle_of_Otranto">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who love thinking or saying, &quot;Uh...wtf?&quot;</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5507063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2906850494906308563">Good old Horace Walpole. Like any literary figure, historians are niggling over the "is he or isn't he" details, but why isn't anyone looking into his freakish obsession with Gothic castles? His goal: "I am going to build a little Gothic castle at Strawberry Hill", and he asked his friends for any fragments of old painted glass, armour, or anything. And thus was born Strawberry Hill, the baby Castle of Otranto.<br/><br/>Otranto (the book) came from that foggy time when novels, while trying to present them</span>
  <span id="freeText2906850494906308563" style="display:none">Good old Horace Walpole. Like any literary figure, historians are niggling over the "is he or isn't he" details, but why isn't anyone looking into his freakish obsession with Gothic castles? His goal: "I am going to build a little Gothic castle at Strawberry Hill", and he asked his friends for any fragments of old painted glass, armour, or anything. And thus was born Strawberry Hill, the baby Castle of Otranto.<br /><br />Otranto (the book) came from that foggy time when novels, while trying to present themselves as sort-of non-fiction, were using plots and dialogue that would be rejected by writers of "Perfect Strangers" fanfic (god forbid such a thing exists). Naturally, I adore it.<br /><br />It starts out with a prince getting crushed by a giant helmet that fell from the sky (really), leading his father to pursue his betrothed, arguing to a priest whether it would be okay to divorce his wife to marry this girl 2/5th of his age who looks almost exactly like his daughter. Then dismembered giant limbs show up around the castle, a woman and a man declare their love for each other for 20 minutes on a castle parapet <i>during</i> a storm <i>while</i> the hero's in some battle. There's some crappy poetry thrown in to break things up, and occult. OCCULT! LUSTING!<br /><br />Hells of funny.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2906850494906308563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="SheAintGotNoShoes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SheAintGotNoShoes" href="/user/show/55625032-sheaintgotnoshoes">SheAintGotNoShoes</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2846824444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15371998198547195892">Three words spring to mind as I type - It's finally over !!<br/><br/>I find it very difficult at times to rate books that were written hundreds of years ago and trying to imagine myself as a reader back then and figuring out what I would have thought of it. It is either imagine myself a woman in 1740 reading this or judging it on how I feel about it as a woman in 2019.<br/><br/>If I go with the latter then I have to give this book a 1.5-2 star rating as it was incredibly tedious. First off the book has teeny print </span>
  <span id="freeText15371998198547195892" style="display:none">Three words spring to mind as I type - It's finally over !!<br /><br />I find it very difficult at times to rate books that were written hundreds of years ago and trying to imagine myself as a reader back then and figuring out what I would have thought of it. It is either imagine myself a woman in 1740 reading this or judging it on how I feel about it as a woman in 2019.<br /><br />If I go with the latter then I have to give this book a 1.5-2 star rating as it was incredibly tedious. First off the book has teeny print which these days annoy me. It also has no paragraphs with any spacing, as well as a complete overabundance of the exclamation point ( probably 20-40 per page ). Coupling all that with the never ending fainting ( men and women ), the constant need to look up the starred words and phrases in the glossary, the total lack of any quotation mark around the dialogue, the overly submissive natures of the women, it was just one big slog thru a sea of molasses.<br /><br />I know it is the first Gothic novel and deemed a classic, but I have gotten to the point where I have to accept that just because it is still in print and a classic, that does not mean I have to like it or find it even mildly enjoyable, which I did not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15371998198547195892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3589655997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3589655997" />
    <a title="Isabella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15819476-isabella"><img alt="Isabella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583250785p2/15819476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3589655997?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabella" href="/user/show/15819476-isabella">Isabella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140437676" href="/book/show/609044.The_Castle_of_Otranto">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15819476-isabella?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3589655997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16758350842147217303">The daddy of gothic fiction, influential to the horror genre as a whole, introducing the classic themes of love, death, suspense & supernatural beings... I'm afraid does not stand the test of time. <br/><br/>The beginning promises an atmospheric tale of mysterious deaths, supernatural occurrences, characters corrupted by their need for complete power, sorrow, and death. But as we keep on reading, the story loses itself in the romance of it all; suddenly there's a love triangle, a damsel in distress, a pri</span>
  <span id="freeText16758350842147217303" style="display:none">The daddy of gothic fiction, influential to the horror genre as a whole, introducing the classic themes of love, death, suspense &amp; supernatural beings... I'm afraid does not stand the test of time. <br /><br />The beginning promises an atmospheric tale of mysterious deaths, supernatural occurrences, characters corrupted by their need for complete power, sorrow, and death. But as we keep on reading, the story loses itself in the romance of it all; suddenly there's a love triangle, a damsel in distress, a prince in disguise, and matters of the heart. <br /><br />I can appreciate Walpole's genius in creating this new literary genre, but I am very glad to see the gothic/horror genre has evolved into something else. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16758350842147217303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_187965851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187965851" />
    <a title="Joseph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5860412-joseph"><img alt="Joseph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549200708p2/5860412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187965851?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph" href="/user/show/5860412-joseph">Joseph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141191959" href="/book/show/6978631-the-castle-of-otranto">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5860412-joseph?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5860412-joseph?shelf=gothic-and-supernatural">gothic-and-supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187965851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12717438501887067539">And so, after having enjoyed several interesting articles about it (most recently <a href='http://www.conceptualfiction.com/the_castle_of_otranto.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>this review</a> by writer and critic Ted Gioa) and after referring to it extensively <a href='http://corymbus.co.uk/sounds-of-horror-the-gothic-in-classical-music/' rel='nofollow noopener'>in a blog post</a> of my own (without ever having actually read it), I finally finished Horace Walpole’s The Castle of Otranto. <br/><br/>Considered in isolation, this slight novel is, frankly, underwhelming, especially to modern readers. A faux-medieval tale of chivalric derring-do and supernatural goings-on in a dark Italian castle, its convoluted</span>
  <span id="freeText12717438501887067539" style="display:none">And so, after having enjoyed several interesting articles about it (most recently <a href="http://www.conceptualfiction.com/the_castle_of_otranto.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> by writer and critic Ted Gioa) and after referring to it extensively <a href="http://corymbus.co.uk/sounds-of-horror-the-gothic-in-classical-music/" rel="nofollow noopener">in a blog post</a> of my own (without ever having actually read it), I finally finished Horace Walpole’s The Castle of Otranto. <br /><br />Considered in isolation, this slight novel is, frankly, underwhelming, especially to modern readers. A faux-medieval tale of chivalric derring-do and supernatural goings-on in a dark Italian castle, its convoluted plot is at best unconvincing and at worst bordering on the unintelligible. The characters are disappointingly two-dimensional, the dialogue overly melodramatic. The otherworldly elements are so unsubtle as to come across as grotesque (the novel starts with Conrad, the heir of a noble family, crushed under a giant plumed helmet which has appeared out of thin air) and the novel’s intentionally humorous streak dashes any chance of us feeling any spine-tingling fear just as surely as the “fearful casque” mangles Conrad’s body.<br /><br />Yet, this 1764 novel deserves respect as (probably) the first Gothic novel, the unlikely instigator of a genre which would give rise to such undoubted masterpieces as, amongst countless others, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18490.Frankenstein" title="Frankenstein by Mary Wollstonecraft Shelley" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankenstein</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51496.The_Strange_Case_of_Dr__Jekyll_and_Mr__Hyde" title="The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde by Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde</a>. The Gothic is a genre that still lives on modern horror and weird fiction and its influences spread well beyond the confines of literature.<br /><br />Seen in this light, The Castle of Otranto starts to reveal merits which might not be immediately obvious. The obsession with the supernatural, the OTT dramatic language, the neo-medievalisms were striking and innovative at the time when the novel was written. What might now seem “facile cliches” (crumbling castles, subterrenean passages, chivalric ideals) would only become “Gothic tropes” after other authors jumped on the Walpole bandwagon. The uncomfortable mix of horror and humour was a peculiarly English trait with roots in Chaucer and Shakespeare. And, underneath the novel’s self-indulgent trappings, there was also an element of radical social critique – the heads of the family come across as abusive, scheming and manipulative; the female characters are not as submissive as (18th century) society might have wanted them to be (Isabella is promised in marriage to the weak Conrad but openly admires other more beautiful knights; Princess Matilda, also pressed into marriage, resists these suggestions and first entertains thoughts of taking the veil then falls in love with a travelling peasant). <br /><br />Walpole’s novel might, in our day and age, be entertaining for all the wrong reasons, but one cannot deny its incredibly far-reaching cultural impact.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://endsoftheword.blogspot.com/2018/10/feat-gothique-review-of-first-gothic.html">https://endsoftheword.blogspot.com/20...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12717438501887067539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rEW8Bz3d06DeNoRQxdxmSCrlfYTykv2Je1qtFKJCYzuRJOOvk/YlMDqq8Pfh/UsJnMX77eelr67VAVgXvnEnhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GVh0OVZO5mkAKtHMw2+JUPAQ8h5al4cTspqJjFo2LKgkOSuR+GUQ+eS2pWvnTqQRRjB0d0+g1TQcwXyPRgVoFw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

The novel follows Victoria\'s progress from spoilt daughter of indulgent aristocrats, through a period of abuse and captivity, to a career of deepening criminality conducted under Satan\'s watchful eye. Charlotte Dacre\'s narrative deftly displays her heroine\'s movement from the vitalized position of Ann Radcliffe\'s heroines to a fully conscious commitment to vice that goes beyond that of \'Monk\' Lewis\'s deluded Ambrosio. The novel\'s most daring aspect is its anatomy of Victoria\'s intense sexual attraction to her Moorish servant Zofloya that transgresses taboos both of class and race. A minor scandal on its first publication, and a significant influence on Byron and Shelley, Zofloya has been unduly neglected. Contradicting idealized stereotypes of women\'s writing, the novel\'s portrait of indulged desire, gratuitous cruelty, and monumental self-absorption retains considerable power to disturb.<\/span>\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8131.Horace_Walpole">About Horace Walpole</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1016452669293843813">Horatio Walpole, 4th Earl of Orford — also known as Horace Walpole — was an English art historian, man of letters, antiquarian and Whig politician. He is now largely remembered for Strawberry Hill, the home he built in Twickenham, south-west London where he revived the Gothic style some decades before his Victorian successors, and for his Gothic novel, <i>The Castle of Otranto</i>. Along with the book, h</span>
  <span id="freeText1016452669293843813" style="display:none">Horatio Walpole, 4th Earl of Orford — also known as Horace Walpole — was an English art historian, man of letters, antiquarian and Whig politician. He is now largely remembered for Strawberry Hill, the home he built in Twickenham, south-west London where he revived the Gothic style some decades before his Victorian successors, and for his Gothic novel, <i>The Castle of Otranto</i>. Along with the book, his literary reputation rests on his <i>Letters</i>, which are of significant social and political interest. He was the son of Sir Robert Walpole, and cousin of Lord Nelson.</span>
